## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is an ODE rate expression for concentration A over time t, typical of chemical kinetics. With only (t, A) available, the most common relationships are mass-action rate laws in A and possibly time-varying rate coefficients or source/sink terms in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited when reactant is abundant)
- Zero-order production: dA_dt = c0 (constant feed or generation of A)
- First-order decay (mass action): dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, dilution, radioactive-like kinetics)
- Linear relaxation to steady state: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (well-mixed CSTR-like balance with constant inflow/production and first-order removal)
- Approach to equilibrium concentration: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward equilibrium/steady concentration c1)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular consumption when the other reactant is effectively proportional to A)
- General n-th order power-law rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global reaction order or lumped kinetics)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type in concentration: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 - c1 * A) (self-amplification at low A with self-limitation at high A)
- Saturating/inhibited consumption (rational form): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (effective saturation or inhibition due to limited capacity/catalyst)
- Mixed source + nonlinear sink: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A**c2 (constant generation with nonlinear removal/consumption)
- Time-varying rate coefficient (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (rate constant changes with time due to aging, ramping conditions)
- Catalyst deactivation / transient activity: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t) (effective rate decreases exponentially in time)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (external cycling in illumination/temperature/flow causing periodic rate modulation)
- Gompertz-type slowing: dA_dt = -c0 * A * log(c1 * A) (decelerating dynamics with logarithmic dependence; can model approach to a limiting state)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- dA_dt proportional to A (dA_dt ∝ -A) indicates first-order kinetics with exponential time-course for A(t).
- dA_dt proportional to A**n (n≠1) suggests mass-action with overall reaction order n or lumped multi-step kinetics.
- A shift (A - c1) in the rate indicates relaxation toward a nonzero equilibrium/steady concentration c1.
- An additive constant term (±c0) in dA_dt implies external feed/production (positive) or constant removal (negative), typical of flow/photolysis/background sources.
- Rational forms like A/(A+c1) indicate saturation or capacity limitation (effective rate flattens at high A).
- Products like A*(1 - c1*A) indicate autocatalysis at low A with self-limitation (finite-capacity or inhibition at higher A).
- Explicit time dependence in the coefficient (c0 + c1*t) implies nonstationary conditions or slowly drifting rate constants.
- Multiplicative exp(-c*t) factors in the rate suggest catalyst/activity decay or transient reactive species availability over time.
- Sin(c*t) modulation indicates periodic forcing (e.g., pulsed operation), which can imprint oscillations on A(t) even without feedback chemistry.

A appears linearly, in a rational saturation (tending to c3 as A→∞ and ~ (c3/c4)A for small A with c4≈11.33), as the base of a sublinear power (c5≈0.631), and inside cos(A*c9); t only appears in exp(c2 t) with c2≈-0.0866. Numerically, the constant and cosine nearly cancel in magnitude (c7≈14.71, c8≈-14.65), the exponential coefficient is sizable and negative (c1≈-0.446), the rational term saturates toward +5.77, and the power term +1.345*A^0.631 provides additional growth while A*c0 is a modest negative linear drift (c0≈-1.05). Approximate simplification: 14.71 - 14.65*cos(0.0527 A) - 1.05*A - 0.446*A*exp(-0.0866 t) + 5.77*A/(A+11.33) + 1.345*A^0.631.

Key structural requirement: the only non-exponential-in-\(t\) part is \(\sin(\sqrt{A})\). None of the candidates explicitly contain \(\sin(\sqrt{A})\); they contain only polynomials/powers in \(A\), rational terms, logs, exponentials, cosines, Abs-powers, and cube-roots. GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: `-0.4466*A*exp(-0.08660*t) + 0.9910*sin(sqrt(A))`**

The GT has two terms:
1. A term proportional to `A*exp(-αt)` (exponential decay in t, linear in A)
2. A term `sin(sqrt(A))` (no t dependence)

Key observation: `sin(sqrt(A))` is a very specific transcendental function. It cannot be represented by polynomials, power laws (`A^c`), `cos(A*c)`, `log(...)`, `exp(A*c)`, rational functions, or `(A*c+1)^(1/3)`.

Let me check which candidates contain `sin(sqrt(A))` or something equivalent:

**None of the candidates contain `sin(...)` explicitly.** So I need to check if any candidate's basis functions can reproduce `sin(sqrt(A))`.

Let me analyze the basis functions present in candidates:
- `A^c` (power law) - cannot equal `sin(sqrt(A))`
- `cos(A*c)` - this is `cos(cA)`, not `sin(sqrt(A))`. These are fundamentally different functions.
- `Abs(A)^c` = `A^c` for A≥0 - power law, cannot equal `sin(sqrt(A))`
- `exp(A*c)` - exponential in A, cannot equal `sin(sqrt(A))`
- `log(A*c+1)` - logarithmic, cannot equal `sin(sqrt(A))`
- `(A*c+1)^(1/3)` - power law, cannot equal `sin(sqrt(A))`
- `A*c/(A+c)` - rational function, cannot equal `sin(sqrt(A))`
- `A^c*d/(A^c+e)` - sigmoid-like, cannot equal `sin(sqrt(A))`
- `A*cos(A*c)` - product of polynomial and cosine, cannot equal `sin(sqrt(A))`

The function `sin(sqrt(A))` is not a polynomial, not a power law, not an exponential, not a logarithm, not a cosine of a linear function, and not a rational function. It's a unique transcendental function that oscillates with decreasing frequency as A increases.

No finite combination of the basis functions available in any candidate (polynomials in A, power laws `A^c`, `cos(cA)`, `exp(cA)`, `log(cA+1)`, rational functions in A, `(cA+1)^{1/3}`) can exactly equal `sin(sqrt(A))` for all A ≥ 0.

Therefore, **none of the candidates can match the GT**.

Let me verify this conclusion by checking each candidate systematically - all candidates use combinations of: `A^n`, `A^c` (fractional powers), `cos(cA)`, `exp(cA)`, `log(cA+1)`, rational functions `A/(A+c)`, `(cA+1)^{1/3}`, `Abs(A)^c`. None include `sin(sqrt(A))` or any function that could produce it.
